The Combined Proof of the Prophet's Perfect Character
Argument from the Prophet's personal qualities as combined evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the combination of the Prophet's moral qualities and personal states constitutes a unique proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's virtues alone do not prove prophethood, but their perfect combination is found only in prophets.

In this passage, the author presents a multifaceted argument for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) by examining his personal character and states before, during, and after his mission. Rather than focusing on a single miracle, the argument draws on the unique combination of virtues—truthfulness, patience, compassion, generosity, courage, and humility—that were consistently manifested throughout his life. As you read, consider why each quality on its own might not suffice, but together they form a compelling sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the English translation. Let the author's detailed description of the Prophet's qualities sink in before analyzing.
Notice how the passage moves from truthfulness to patience, then to specific virtues like compassion and courage.
2
Identify the enumerated qualities
List the distinct qualities the author mentions: truthfulness, patience, steadfastness after power, compassion, generosity, disregard for worldly temptations, humility with the poor, dignity with the rich, wise rulings, and courage.
These are not random virtues; they cover all aspects of human conduct.
3
Understand why each alone is insufficient
The author states that each quality individually does not prove prophethood, because non-prophets can also possess one of these virtues to some degree. Reflect on why this is true.
For example, many people are generous, but not to the extent and with the combination found in the Prophet.
4
Appreciate the combined argument
The key point is that the perfect combination of all these qualities in one person is unprecedented and can only come from a prophet. Notice how the author emphasizes this with the phrase 'their combination is something that is not obtained except for prophets.'
This is the core of the lesson: the whole is greater than the sum of its parts.
5
Consider the objection and response
The author addresses a potential objection: philosophers also exhibit amazing morals. The response is that their virtues are not combined in the way that produces a prophet's transformative impact. Read the commentary for clarification.
This shows the depth of the argument—anticipating and refuting counterexamples.

الفقهية ( وإقدامه حيث يحجم الأبطال ) فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يفر قط من أعدائه وإن عظم الخوف مثل يوم ويوم الأحزاب وذلك يدل على قوة قلبه وشهامة جنانه ( ولولا ثقته بعصمة الله إياه من الناس ) كما وعدها بقوله والله يعصمك من الناس ﴾ [المائدة : ٦٧] ( لامتنع ذلك عادة وأنه ) عطف على إقدامه المندرج في المجزورات الداخلة في حيز الاستدلال أي وبأنه (لم يتلون حاله وقد تلونت به الأحوال ) ثم بين قوله بأحواله وما عطف عليه بقوله : ( من أمور من تتبعها علم أن كل واحد منها وإن كان لا يدل على نبوته ) لأن امتياز شخص بمزيد فضيلة عن سائر الأشخاص لا يدل على كونه نبياً ( لكن مجموعها مما لا يحصل إلا للأنبياء) قطعا فاجتماع هذه الصفات في ذاته عليه الصلاة والسلام من أعظم الدلائل على نبوته وعلى ما قررناه ) فلايرد ما يحكى عن أفاضل الحكماء من الأخلاق العجيبة التي جعلها الناس قدوة لأحوالهم في الدنيا والآخرة . قوله : ( جوامع الكلم أي الكلم الجوامع للبلاغة. قوله : (باخع نفسك ) بخع نفسه بخعاً قتله غماً . قوله : ( يجحم الأبطال) بتقديم الجيم على الحاء المهملة وعكسه أي يتأخر عن الحرب . قوله : (وشهامة جنانه شهم الرجل بالضم ،شهامة، فهو شهم أي جلد ذكي الفؤاد والجنان بفتح الجيم القلب .
The First Observatory - The Fourth Objective: On Proving the Prophethood of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, named 'The Guide from Error' (The argument from his states before prophethood, at the time of the call, and after its completion). That is, he, peace and blessings be upon him, never lied at all, neither in important religious matters nor in important worldly matters. If he had lied once, he would have been contradicted, as he said: 'I have been given the comprehensive words.' He endured various hardships in delivering the message and bore them patiently without any slackening in his resolve. When he gained mastery over his enemies and attained a high rank in the execution of his command over wealth and lives, he did not change from what he was; rather, he remained from the beginning of his life to its end on a single praiseworthy path. (And his great character) for he, peace and blessings be upon him, was extremely compassionate toward his community until he was addressed by His saying: 'So do not let yourself be consumed in grief over them' [Fatir: 8], and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief over their departure' [Al-Kahf: 6]. He was extremely generous until he was rebuked by His saying: 'And do not stretch your hand out completely' [Al-Isra: 29]. He paid no attention to the adornments of this world, so much so that Quraysh offered him wealth, a wife, and leadership to abandon his claim, but he did not heed them. He was extremely humble with the poor and needy, and extremely dignified with the wealthy and the rich. (And his wise rulings which are detailed in books of jurisprudence. And his courage where the brave hold back.) He, peace and blessings be upon him, never fled from his enemies, no matter how great the fear, such as on the day or the day of the Confederates. That indicates the strength of his heart and the bravery of his soul. (Were it not for his confidence in God's protection of him from people) as He promised him with His saying: 'And God will protect you from people' [Al-Ma'idah: 67], (that would ordinarily be impossible. And that) is connected to his courage included among the qualities entering into the scope of the argument, i.e., and that (his state did not change while states changed around him). Then he clarified his statement 'by his states' and what is connected to it by his saying: (Among things from which one who investigates them knows that each one of them, even if it does not indicate his prophethood) because a person's being distinguished by an additional virtue over other people does not indicate that he is a prophet, (yet their combination is something that is not obtained except for prophets) definitively. So the gathering of these attributes in his person, peace and blessings be upon him, is among the greatest proofs of his prophethood, according to what we have established. (So there is no refutation from what is narrated about the eminent philosophers of amazing morals which people have taken as exemplars for their states in this world and the Hereafter.) His saying: 'comprehensive words' means the words that are comprehensive of eloquence. His saying: 'killing yourself with grief' means he killed himself with grief. His saying: 'where the brave hold back' with the letter jim before the letter ha without dots, and its opposite, means he stayed behind from battle. His saying: 'the bravery of his soul' – 'shahima' the man with damma, 'shahama', so he is 'shahim', meaning strong, intelligent of heart, and 'al-jinan' with the letter jim fatiha means the heart.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from the Prophet's personal qualities before and after his mission. It begins by establishing his perfect truthfulness in both religious and worldly matters, citing his own statement 'I have been given the comprehensive words' to indicate his eloquence and divine support. It then lists his patience in delivering the message, his unwavering resolve, and his complete lack of change after gaining power—unlike typical human behavior. The author then enumerates his great moral qualities: extreme compassion for his community (supported by Quranic verses), extreme generosity, disregard for worldly temptations, humility with the poor, dignity with the rich, wise rulings, and unparalleled courage in battle (even when others fled). The argument emphasizes that each quality individually might not prove prophethood, but their combination in one person is something that only prophets possess. The author also notes that had the Prophet not been assured of divine protection, his courage would have been impossible. Finally, the author addresses a potential objection: the amazing morals of philosophers are not comparable because they are single virtues, not a comprehensive combination that produces a prophet's transformative impact. The footnotes clarify key terms like 'jawaami' al-kalim' (comprehensive words) and 'bakh'a nafsahu' (killing himself with grief).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that each individual virtue of the Prophet is enough to prove his prophethood.
Correction: The passage clarifies that each virtue alone does not indicate prophethood, because non-prophets can also have one of these virtues. It is the perfect combination that is exclusive to prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author considers the Prophet's personal qualities as evidence for prophethood?
A) Each individual quality is extraordinary.
B) The combination of all these qualities is found only in prophets.
C) The Prophet was the most generous person.
D) The Prophet never fled from battle.

Key Takeaway
The unique combination of perfect virtues in the Prophet Muhammad is a clear sign that he was a true prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the Prophet's virtues combine uniquely. Which of these virtues do you lack most, and what one concrete action will you take today to begin cultivating it?
?
The Prophet did not change after gaining power. When have you found yourself adopting different behavior after gaining authority or recognition? How can you realign yourself with the consistency of the Prophet starting now?
?
The Prophet was rebuked for excessive generosity. Are you more inclined to stinginess or over-giving? What step can you take this week to mirror the prophetic balance, and to whom will you extend that kindness?

Third Argument: Predictions of Previous Prophets
Author presents and refutes the prediction argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why predictions from earlier scriptures are not a sufficient proof of prophethood and why miracles are the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Biblical predictions are not the main proof; miracles are.

This lesson presents the third argument for prophethood: the predictions of earlier prophets. The author raises objections showing that such predictions are either absent in detail or too general, and could refer to someone else. He then clarifies that the real proof is miracles, and these arguments are only supplementary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the structure: argument, two objections, and the author's answer.
Pay attention to the parentheses indicating objections.
2
Identify the two objections
Find the two specific objections raised against using predictions as proof: (1) detailed description is missing, (2) general mention could refer to another person.
The first objection is about detailed vs. general description.
3
Understand the author's answer
Notice that the author shifts the focus to miracles as the primary proof and relegates predictions to a minor role.
The phrase 'المعتمد' (the relied-upon) is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( والمسلك الثالث : ) من تلك المسالك ( إخبار الأنبياء المتقدمين عليه عن نبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام في التوراة والإنجيل فإن قيل : إن زعمتم مجيء صفته مفصلاً أنه يجيء في السنة الفلانية في البلدة الفلانية وصفته كيت وكيت فاعلموا أنه نبي فباطل لأنا نجد التوراة والإنجيل خاليين عن ذلك، وأما ذكره مجملاً فإن سلم فلا يدل على النبوة بل على ظهور إنسان كامل) فلا يجديكم نفعاً ( أو ) نقول : على تقدير تسليم دلالته على النبوة (لعله شخص آخر لم يظهر بعد ( فلا يثبت مدعاكم . ( قلنا : المعتمد ) في إثبات نبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام كما مر ) ظهور المعجزة على يده وهذه الوجوه الأخر للتكملة وزيارة التقرير.
(And the third path:) from among those paths (the informing of the earlier prophets about his prophethood, peace and blessings be upon him, in the Torah and the Gospel. For if it is said: If you claim the coming of his description in detail, that he will come in such-and-such a year, in such-and-such a town, and his description is such-and-such, then know that he is a prophet – this is false, because we find the Torah and the Gospel empty of that. As for his mention in general terms, even if conceded, it does not indicate prophethood but rather the appearance of a perfect man) so it does not benefit you. (Or) we say: on the assumption of conceding its indication of prophethood, (perhaps it is another person who has not yet appeared) so it does not prove your claim. (We say: The relied-upon) in proving his prophethood, peace and blessings be upon him, as has passed (is the appearance of a miracle at his hand, and these other aspects are for completion and reinforcement of the argument.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument for prophethood: the predictions of earlier prophets in the Torah and Gospel. The author first states the argument, then immediately raises two objections. The first objection: if the predictions were detailed (specific year, place, description), then we would accept, but the Torah and Gospel are empty of such detail. General mention is conceded but does not prove prophethood—only the appearance of a perfect man. The second objection: even if the general mention indicated prophethood, it could refer to another person not yet appeared. Thus, these predictions do not prove the claim. The author then gives the answer: the real proof is the appearance of miracles at his hand; these other arguments are only supplementary. This shows that the author considers the miracle argument primary.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Biblical predictions are a primary proof of prophethood.
Correction: The passage clarifies that predictions are not a decisive proof; the primary proof is miracles.

Checkpoint

B) Because they are either not present in detail or only general, and could refer to someone else.
C) Because the Torah and Gospel are corrupted.
D) Because the Prophet himself rejected them.

Key Takeaway
The predictions of earlier prophets are not a decisive proof; miracles are the true evidence of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You may have heard arguments from other scriptures. But the author says the real proof is a miracle. Have you personally witnessed the miracle of the Quran? If not, what is stopping you from seeking it as evidence?

The Fourth Argument: Social Transformation as Proof of Prophethood
Imam al-Razi's proof from the transformation of a corrupt society.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's argument that the Prophet's transformation of a corrupt society from false religions to monotheism and moral perfection demonstrates his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's completion of noble morals is the very essence of prophethood.

Imam al-Razi presents a powerful argument that goes beyond miracles. He asks us to look at the state of the pre-Islamic world and the profound transformation the Prophet brought. This argument is based on the very meaning of prophethood itself.

Guided Path
1
Examine the pre-Islamic state
Read the description of the people to whom the Prophet was sent: they had no book, no wisdom, and were divided into false religions.
Notice the diversity of corruption: idolatry, anthropomorphism, dualism, trinity.
2
Identify the Prophet's claim and mission
The Prophet claimed to be sent with the Book and wisdom to complete noble morals and perfect people in belief and action.
3
Observe the transformation achieved
The Prophet succeeded: false religions vanished, monotheism and transcendence spread. This is a historical fact.
This transformation is not a small change but a complete reversal.
4
Understand the conclusion
The text concludes that this transformation is the very meaning of prophethood: perfecting human souls and treating heart diseases.
The argument links the effect (transformation) to the essence of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( المسلك الرابع : ( وارتضاه الإمام الرازي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ادعى بين قوم لا كتاب لهم ولا حكمة فيهم ( بل كانوا معرضين عن الحق معتكفين إما على عبادة الأوثان كمشركي العرب وإما على دين التشبيه وصنعة التزوير وترويج الأكاذيب المفتريات كاليهود وإما على عبادة الإلهين ونكاح المحارم كالمجوس، وإما على القول بالأب والابن والتثليث كالنصارى ( إني بعثت ) من عند الله ( بالكتاب ) المنير ( والحكمة ( الباهرة لأتمم مكارم الأخلاق وأكمل الناس في قوتهم العلمية ) بالعقائد الحقة ( والعملية) بالأعمال الصالحة ( وأنور العالم بالإيمان والعمل الصالح ففعل ذلك وأظهر دينه على الدين كله كما وعده الله فاضمحلت تلك الأديان الزائعة وزالت المقالات الفاسدة وأشرقت شموس التوحيد وأقمار التنزيه في أقطار الآفاق ولا معنى للنبوة إلا ذلك ) فإن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام هو الذي يكمل النفوس البشرية ويعالج الأمراض القلبية التي هي غالبة على أكثر النفوس فلا بد لهم من طبيب يعالجهم ولما كان تأثير دعوة محمد الله في علاج القلوب المريضة وأزالت ظلماتها أكمل وأتم وجب القطع بكونه نبياً هو أفضل الأنبياء والرسل. قال الإمام الرازي في المطالب العالية وهذا برهان ظاهر من باب برهان اللم فإنا بحثنا عن حقيقة النبوة وبينا أن تلك الماهية لم تحصل لأحد كما حصلت له عليه الصلاة والسلام فيكون أفضل عداه . وأما إثباتها بالمعجزة فمن باب برهان الآن قال المصنف : ( وهذا ) المسلك قريب من مسلك (الحكماء ) إذ حاصله أن الناس في معاشهم ومعادهم محتاجون إلى يضع لهم قانوناً يسعدهم في الدارين ) واعلم أن المنكرين لبعثه عليه الصلاة والسلام خاصة قومان: أحدهما: القادحون في معجزته كالنصارى وقد مر. قوله : (لا كتاب لهم هذا بالنسبة إلى مشركي العرب خاصة، وإن كانت البعثة عامة. :قوله من باب برهان الله قيل : البرهان اللمي هو الاستدلال بالعلة على المعلول وكون ما ذكر من تتميم مكارم الأخلاق وغيره علة للنبوة إنما يظهر على أصل الحكيم وأما على أصل المتكلمين فلا لا أن يحمل على العلة العادية .
(The fourth path:) which Imam al-Razi approved, that he, peace and blessings be upon him, claimed among a people who had no book and no wisdom among them (rather they were turning away from truth, adhering either to the worship of idols like the Arab polytheists, or to the religion of anthropomorphism and the craft of falsification and spreading lies and fabrications like the Jews, or to the worship of two gods and marriage of relatives like the Magians, or to the belief in the Father, Son, and Trinity like the Christians) (I have been sent) from God (with the Book) luminous (and Wisdom) dazzling (to complete noble morals and perfect people in their theoretical strength) with true beliefs (and practical strength) with righteous deeds (and to illuminate the world with faith and righteous deed. So he did that and made his religion prevail over all religion as God promised him. So those deviant religions vanished, the corrupt ideas disappeared, and the suns of monotheism and moons of transcendence shone in the regions of the horizons. And there is no meaning of prophethood except that.) For the prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, is the one who perfects human souls and treats heart diseases that dominate most souls. So they necessarily need a physician to treat them. And since the effect of Muhammad's call, may God bless him and grant him peace, in treating sick hearts and removing their darkness was the most complete and perfect, it is necessary to conclude that he is a prophet and the best of prophets and messengers. Imam al-Razi said in al-Matālib al-ʿĀliyya: This is a manifest proof from the category of proof of why (burhān limmī), for we investigated the reality of prophethood and showed that that essence was not attained by anyone as it was attained by him, peace and blessings be upon him, so he is the best besides him. As for proving it by miracle, it is from the category of proof of that (burhān innī). The author said: (This) path is close to the path of the philosophers, for its conclusion is that people, in their livelihood and their afterlife, are in need of one who lays down a law for them that makes them happy in both abodes. And know that the deniers of his mission, peace and blessings be upon him, specifically are two groups: one of them are those who attack his miracle like the Christians, and it has passed. His saying: 'no book for them' is specific to the Arab polytheists, even though the mission was general. His saying: 'from the category of proof of God' – it is said: The proof of why (burhān limmī) is inference from cause to effect, and that what is mentioned of completing noble morals and other things being a cause for prophethood appears only according to the principle of the philosopher. As for according to the principle of the theologians, it is not, unless it is interpreted as a customary cause.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument for prophethood, approved by Imam al-Razi. It begins by describing the pre-Islamic state of the people to whom the Prophet was sent: they had no divine book, no true wisdom, and were immersed in various false religions (idolatry, anthropomorphism, dualism, trinity). The Prophet claimed to be sent by God with the Book and wisdom to complete noble morals, perfect people in knowledge and action, and illuminate the world. He succeeded: all false religions vanished, and monotheism spread. The argument concludes that this transformation is the very meaning of prophethood—a prophet is a physician of hearts, perfecting souls. Since Muhammad's impact was the most complete, he must be a prophet and the best. Imam al-Razi notes that this is a proof from cause to effect (burhān limmī): we first understand the essence of prophethood, then see that it is fully realized in Muhammad. In contrast, proving prophethood by miracles is from effect to cause (burhān innī). The author notes that this argument is similar to the philosophers' argument that people need a lawgiver for happiness. Finally, the author mentions two groups of deniers: those who attack the miracle (like Christians) and another group referenced earlier. The footnotes clarify that the description 'no book' applies specifically to the Arab polytheists, and that the causal argument works on philosophers' principles but not on theologians' unless taken as customary cause.

Key Terms
المسلك الرابع
مكارم الأخلاق
حقيقة النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, why is the transformation of society by the Prophet considered a proof of prophethood?
A) Because it demonstrates his political power.
B) Because it shows he perfectly fulfilled the essence of prophethood, which is to perfect human souls.
C) Because it was predicted in previous scriptures.
D) Because he performed a miracle.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's transformation of society proves his prophethood because he actualized the very purpose of prophethood: perfecting human souls.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet was sent to complete noble morals. Which specific moral virtue are you neglecting today that would bring you closer to the purpose of his mission? What is one concrete step you will take this week to embody it?
?
Before Islam, people were stuck in false beliefs and corrupt practices. What false belief or harmful habit are you still clinging to despite knowing it contradicts the suns of monotheism that have already illuminated your heart? How will you uproot it starting today?
?
The argument shows that prophethood is about transforming souls—theoretical and practical. When was the last time you felt your soul genuinely transformed by the message of the Prophet, or are you merely going through religious motions? What would a real transformation look like for you right now?

The Logical Structure: Burhān Limmī and the Philosophers' Approach
Classification of the proof as burhān limmī and comparison to philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between burhān limmī and burhān innī and how Imam al-Razi's argument is a limmī proof, as well as its connection to the philosophers' need for a lawgiver.

Core Idea
Knowing the essence of prophethood makes the proof from transformation a cause-to-effect demonstration.

Imam al-Razi not only presents the argument but also clarifies its epistemological status. He explains that this is a proof from cause to effect (burhān limmī), unlike miracles which are from effect to cause. This lesson explores that distinction and how this argument aligns with the philosophers' reasoning about the need for a prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the proof classification
The passage begins by describing the Prophet as a physician of hearts, then al-Razi classifies the argument as burhān limmī.
2
Understand burhān limmī vs burhān innī
Burhān limmī infers from cause to effect; burhān innī goes from effect to cause. Al-Razi says this argument is limmī because we start from the essence of prophethood.
This is a key distinction in Islamic logic.
3
Note the similarity to philosophers
The author notes that this path is close to the philosophers' argument that people need a lawgiver for happiness in both worlds.
This shows a convergence between kalam and falsafa.
4
Consider the deniers and clarifications
Two groups deniers: one attacks the miracle. Also a footnote clarifies 'no book' applies to Arab polytheists specifically.
The footnote helps avoid misunderstanding.

The Fourth Proof: Muhammad's Transformation as Evidence of Prophethood
Sanusi presents al-Razi's proof from Muhammad's transformation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the transformative impact of Muhammad's mission serves as a rational proof of his prophethood, and how this differs from proof by miracle.

Core Idea
Muhammad's success in transforming a corrupt society is itself a proof of prophethood.

Imam al-Razi presented a powerful argument for prophethood based not on supernatural miracles but on the observable transformation of a people. This passage outlines how Muhammad's mission turned a fragmented, misguided society into a monotheistic community, fulfilling the very purpose of prophethood. We will explore this proof and its logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with context
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the description of the people before Islam—they were without scripture and wisdom, divided into corrupt groups.
The passage uses parenthetical insertions to clarify each group's beliefs.
2
Identify the core argument
Find the sentence that states the proof: that Muhammad transformed the people, made false religions vanish, and spread monotheism. This is the empirical basis.
The key is that this transformation happened despite the initial corruption.
3
Understand the definition of prophethood
The passage defines prophethood as perfecting souls and treating heart diseases. This establishes the criterion for judging prophetic claims.
Prophethood is like a physician for souls.
4
Distinguish the two types of proof
The author contrasts proof from cause (burhan limmi) with proof from effect (burhan anni). The transformation proof is burhan limmi, while miracle-based proof is burhan anni.
Burhan limmi goes from essence to manifestation; burhan anni goes from sign to signified.
5
Connect to the philosophers
Note the resemblance to the philosophical argument that humanity needs a lawgiver for happiness in both abodes.
This shows the rational continuity between revealed and philosophical proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك الرابع : ( وارتضاه الإمام الرازي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ادعى بين قوم لا كتاب لهم ولا حكمة فيهم ( بل كانوا معرضين عن الحق معتكفين إما على عبادة الأوثان كمشركي العرب وإما على دين التشبيه وصنعة التزوير وترويج الأكاذيب المفتريات كاليهود وإما على عبادة الإلهين ونكاح المحارم كالمجوس، وإما على القول بالأب والابن والتثليث كالنصارى ( إني بعثت ) من عند الله ( بالكتاب ) المنير ( والحكمة ( الباهرة لأتمم مكارم الأخلاق وأكمل الناس في قوتهم العلمية ) بالعقائد الحقة ( والعملية) بالأعمال الصالحة ( وأنور العالم بالإيمان والعمل الصالح ففعل ذلك وأظهر دينه على الدين كله كما وعده الله فاضمحلت تلك الأديان الزائعة وزالت المقالات الفاسدة وأشرقت شموس التوحيد وأقمار التنزيه في أقطار الآفاق ولا معنى للنبوة إلا ذلك ) فإن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام هو الذي يكمل النفوس البشرية ويعالج الأمراض القلبية التي هي غالبة على أكثر النفوس فلا بد لهم من طبيب يعالجهم ولما كان تأثير دعوة محمد الله في علاج القلوب المريضة وأزالت ظلماتها أكمل وأتم وجب القطع بكونه نبياً هو أفضل الأنبياء والرسل. قال الإمام الرازي في المطالب العالية وهذا برهان ظاهر من باب برهان اللم فإنا بحثنا عن حقيقة النبوة وبينا أن تلك الماهية لم تحصل لأحد كما حصلت له عليه الصلاة والسلام فيكون أفضل عداه . وأما إثباتها بالمعجزة فمن باب برهان الآن قال المصنف : ( وهذا ) المسلك قريب من مسلك (الحكماء ) إذ حاصله أن الناس في معاشهم ومعادهم محتاجون إلى يضع لهم قانوناً يسعدهم في الدارين )
The fourth path: (and it was approved by Imam al-Razi that he, peace and blessings be upon him, claimed among a people who had no scripture and no wisdom among them (rather they were averse to the truth, adhering either to idol worship like the Arab polytheists, or to the religion of anthropomorphism and the practice of forgery and promotion of lies and slanders like the Jews, or to worship of two gods and incest like the Magians, or to belief in Father, Son, and Trinity like the Christians) (I have been sent) from God (with the luminous Book) (and the brilliant wisdom) to perfect noble morals and to complete people in their theoretical power (with true beliefs) and practical power (with righteous deeds) and to illuminate the world with faith and righteous deeds. He did that and manifested his religion over all religion as God promised him, so those stray religions vanished and the corrupt doctrines disappeared, and the suns of monotheism and the moons of transcendence shone in the horizons of the world. There is no meaning of prophethood except that.) For the prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, is the one who perfects human souls and treats heart diseases that prevail in most souls, so they must have a physician to treat them. Since the effect of Muhammad's call, may God bless him, in treating sick hearts and removing their darknesses was more complete and perfect, it is necessary to conclude that he is a prophet and the best of the prophets and messengers. Imam al-Razi said in al-Matalib al-‘Aliyya: This is an apparent proof of the type of demonstration of the reason (burhan limmi); we investigated the reality of prophethood and showed that that essence was not attained by anyone as it was attained by him, so he is superior to all others. As for proving it by miracle, that is of the type of demonstration of the fact (burhan anni). The author said: (And this) path is close to the path of the philosophers, for its gist is that people in their livelihood and afterlife are in need of one who lays down for them a law that makes them happy in both abodes.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof of Muhammad's prophethood, which is attributed to Imam al-Razi. It begins by describing the condition of the people among whom Muhammad claimed prophethood: they were devoid of scripture and wisdom, divided into various corrupt groups (polytheists, anthropomorphists, dualists, trinitarians). Despite this, Muhammad claimed to be sent with a book and wisdom to perfect moral character and complete people in knowledge and practice. He succeeded in transforming them, eradicating false religions and spreading monotheism. The argument then defines prophethood as the perfection of souls and treatment of spiritual diseases, and since Muhammad's mission accomplished this most effectively, he is necessarily a prophet and the best of prophets. The passage then clarifies that this is a proof from the cause (burhan limmi): it examines the essence of prophethood and shows that Muhammad fulfilled it perfectly. In contrast, proof by miracle is from effect to cause (burhan anni). Finally, the author notes that this proof resembles the philosophers' argument that humanity needs a lawgiver for happiness in this life and the afterlife.

Key Terms
المسلك الرابع
برهان اللم
برهان الآن
النبوة
مكارم الأخلاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proof from transformation is the same as proof from miracle.
Correction: This proof is a burhan limmi (demonstration of the cause), while miracle-based proof is burhan anni (demonstration from effect). They are different logical types.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, what is the primary evidence for Muhammad's prophethood?
A) His performance of physical miracles
B) His transformation of a corrupt society into a righteous one
C) His claim to have a book from God
D) His superior lineage

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's transformation of a corrupt society into a righteous one is a rational proof of his prophethood, distinct from miracle-based proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage describes people 'averse to the truth, adhering to idol worship, anthropomorphism, dualism, trinitarianism' before Muhammad. Examine yourself: in what subtle ways are you still 'averse to the truth'—fleeing from a command of Allah or rationalizing a sin? What specific step will you take today to let the message of Muhammad uproot that darkness?
?
Muhammad's call 'treated sick hearts' and 'removed darknesses.' Has your heart been healed by his message, or are you still carrying spiritual diseases like pride, envy, or heedlessness? If you were to honestly assess, what portion of your heart has truly been illuminated by the 'suns of monotheism'? Name one darkness you will ask Allah to remove tonight.
?
The proof of prophethood lies in the actual transformation it brings. If your life were compared to the pre-Islamic society—filled with corruption and falsehood—what evidence would there be that you have genuinely accepted Muhammad as your prophet? Are you more concerned with changing others or with letting his message transform your own character right now?

Refuting the Jewish Objection on Abrogation
Jews' first objection against Muhammad's prophethood (abrogation) is refuted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jewish objection that abrogation implies divine ignorance or change (badā') is refuted using Ashʿarī principles.

Core Idea
Abrogation reflects changing benefits, not divine ignorance or regret.

The Jews argued that Muhammad's prophethood abrogates previous law, which would imply God was ignorant or changed His mind. This lesson presents the Ashʿarī response: divine rulings are not necessarily tied to benefit, and even if they are, benefits change over time. The passage also notes that previous laws were for different peoples.

Guided Path
1
Read and locate the objection
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note how the Jews argue that abrogation implies either ignorance or badā'.
2
Understand the two implications
The Jews say abrogation either means God was unaware of a benefit (ignorance) or He changed His mind without reason (badā'). Both are impossible for God.
These are the two horns of the dilemma.
3
First rejoinder: Ashʿarī view on benefit
The text answers that according to Ashʿarī theology, it is not necessary that rulings contain a benefit. So the assumption that rulings must have a benefit is rejected.
4
Second rejoinder: changing benefits over time
Even if benefit is required, benefits can change with time, like medicine. So abrogation reflects a new benefit, not ignorance or change.
5
Note the final argument: different subjects
The abrogated laws were for previous peoples; the current law is for a different community, so no contradiction arises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المنكرين لبعثه عليه الصلاة والسلام خاصة قومان: أحدهما: القادحون في معجزته كالنصارى وقد مر ما فيه كفاية ) لدفع مقالتهم ( وثانيهما : اليهود إلا العيسوية ) منهم ( فإنهم سلموا بعثته لكن إلى العرب خاصة لا إلى الخلق كافة واحتجوا أي اليهود المنكرون . (بوجهين : الأول : أن نبوته تقتضي نسخ دين ( من قبله ) إذ قد خالفهم في كثير من الأحكام الشرعية العملية ( باتفاق منكم لكن النسخ) أمر ( محال لأنه يدل ) إما ( على الجهل أو البداء وكلاهما محال على الله تعالى بيانه أنه ( لا بد أن يكون الحكم الصادر عنه تعالى مشتملا على مصلحة لئلا يلزم الترجيح بلا مرجح وحينئذ ( لو كان فيه ) أي في الحكم المنسوخ (مصلحة لا يعلمها ) أي لا يعلم فواتها بنسخه فلذلك نسخه فالجهل وإن كان يعلمها فرأى رعايتها أولاً ثم أهملها بلا سبب ثانياً فالبداء) أي الندم عما كان يفعل ) والجواب : أنه لا يجب رعاية (المصلحة) في الأحكام ( عندنا ) فلا يلزم اشتمال الحكم المنسوخ على مصلحة ( وإن وجب) أن تراعى المصالح في الاحكام فربما حدثت مصلحة لم تكن حاصلة قبل فإن المصالح تختلف بحسب الأوقات كشرب الدواء الخاص في وقت دون وقت فربما كانت المصلحة في وقت ثبوت الحكم لاشتماله فيه على ما يجب رعايته ( وفي ) وقت (آخر ارتفاعه ) لاشتماله فيه على مصلحة أخرى حادثة بعد زوال الأولى أو مرجوحيتها مقيسة إلى الثانية فلا يلزم ما ذكرتم من الجهل أو البداء ( وكيف) لا يجوز ما ذكرناه ( والمحكوم عليه هنا ) أي في نسخ شرائع من قبلنا بشريعتنا ( ليس بمتحد ) إذ تلك لأقوام آخرين
Know that the deniers of his mission, peace and blessings be upon him, are specifically two groups: One: those who attack his miracle, like the Christians, and what suffices to refute their claim has passed. The second: the Jews, except for the ‘Isawiyya among them, for they accepted his mission but only to the Arabs specifically, not to all creation. And the deniers among the Jews argued with two points: The first: that his prophethood requires the abrogation of the religion before him, since he contradicted them in many practical legal rulings, by your agreement, but abrogation is impossible because it indicates either ignorance or badā’ (change of mind), both of which are impossible for God. Its explanation: the ruling coming from God must contain a benefit (maslaha) to avoid preponderance without a preponderator. Then if in the abrogated ruling there was a benefit of which He was unaware—meaning unaware of its loss by abrogating it, so He abrogated it—that is ignorance. And if He was aware of it, and first saw fit to preserve it, then abandoned it without a second cause, that is badā’ (regret for what was done). The answer: It is not necessary to consider benefit in rulings according to us, so the abrogated ruling need not contain a benefit. And if it is necessary to consider benefits in rulings, perhaps a benefit arose that was not present before; for benefits differ according to times, like drinking a specific medicine at one time and not another. Perhaps the benefit lay in the time of establishing the ruling due to its containing what must be observed, and at another time its removal due to its containing another benefit that occurred after the first ceased, or its inferiority compared to the second. So what you mentioned of ignorance or badā’ does not follow. And how could what we have said not be permissible, while the subject of the ruling here—that is, in abrogating the laws before us by our law—is not identical, for those were for other peoples?
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage refutes the first objection of the Jews against Muhammad's prophethood. The Jews argue that his prophethood requires abrogation of previous laws, and abrogation is impossible because it would imply either ignorance (if God didn't know the benefit would be lost) or badā' (change of mind, if He knew but changed His mind without reason), both of which are impossible for God. The answer provides two rejoinders: First, according to the Ash'ari position, it is not necessary that divine rulings be based on considerations of benefit (maslaha), so abrogation does not imply ignorance or change. Second, even if one holds that rulings must consider benefit, benefits can change over time, so a ruling may be beneficial at one time and its abrogation beneficial at another. Additionally, the abrogation of previous laws for other peoples does not affect the current community, as the subjects are different.

Key Terms
النسخ
المصلحة
البداء
الجهل
العيسوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That abrogation means God changed His mind or acted ignorantly.
Correction: The passage explains that abrogation does not imply ignorance or badā' because benefits are not necessary for rulings (Ashʿarī view) or because benefits can change over time.

Checkpoint
What is the first rejoinder to the Jewish objection that abrogation implies ignorance or badā'?
A) Abrogation is not possible in the first place
B) God's rulings need not be based on benefit (maslaha)
C) The Jews themselves accept abrogation in their own scripture
D) Muhammad did not actually abrogate the previous laws

Key Takeaway
The Jewish objection that abrogation implies divine ignorance or change is refuted by showing that rulings need not be based on benefit, and benefits can change over time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a truth because it didn't fit your previous understanding, like the Jews rejected Muhammad due to abrogation? What evidence would make you reconsider a firmly held belief?
?
The Ashʿarī response shows that benefits change with time. Is there a practice or opinion you cling to that may no longer be beneficial? Are you willing to let go when wisdom requires it?
?
The objection claimed abrogation shows God's ignorance or regret. Do you truly trust that God's decisions are wise even when they seem inconsistent from your limited perspective? How can you cultivate that trust?

The Impossibility of Moses Explicitly Denying Abrogation
Al-Jurjani refutes the claim that Moses negated abrogation using tawatur reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Jurjani argues that Moses could not have explicitly stated the non-permanence of his religion, and why the absence of tawatur disproves the Jewish claim.

Core Idea
If Moses had denied abrogation, it would be known to all — its absence proves the claim false.

In this refutation, al-Jurjani systematically dismantles Jewish arguments for the permanence of Mosaic law. He examines the claim that Moses himself negated abrogation and considers three possibilities: explicit permanence, explicit non-permanence, or silence. Both non-permanence and silence are invalid, with non-permanence requiring tawatur that is absent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
The passage contains embedded objections and responses.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage presents three possibilities regarding Moses' statement about his religion's permanence. Find each one and note how al-Jurjani evaluates them.
3
Understand the tawatur argument
Al-Jurjani argues that if Moses had explicitly stated non-permanence, it would have been massively transmitted (tawatur). Ask yourself why that is required and why its absence is significant.
This is a key logical move in kalam.
4
Examine the refutation of the Sabbath claim
See how al-Jurjani denies the tawatur of the Sabbath's permanence and mentions its fabrication by Ibn al-Rawandi.
This counters the Jewish proof text.
5
Connect to the overall lesson
Reflect on how this passage demonstrates the use of tawatur and logical disjunction in theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه لنا ولك أن تحمل المحكوم عليه هاهنا على الفعل فإن ما يتعلق به الحكم الناسخ الأفعال مغاير لما تعلق به الحكم المفسوخ وحينئذ يجوز النسخ في الأحكام المتعلقة بأفعال شخص واحد . ( الثاني : ( من الوجهين ( أن موسى عليه السلام نفي نسخ دينه ولا بد من الاعتراف بصدقه لكونه نبياً) بالاتفاق وحينئذ لا نبوة من يدعي نسخه وهو المطلوب (بيانه ) أي بيان أنه نفى نسخ دينه ( أنه تواتر عنه ) . قوله : ( تمسكوا بالسبت ما دامت السماوات والأرض وإذا ثبت دوام السبت وامتناع نسخه ثبت امتناعه في سائر أحكامه، بل نقول : المراد بدوامه دوام اليهودية كما يتبادر إليه الفهم ( وأيضاً ) فإنه (إما أن يكون ) موسى (قد صرح بدوام دينه أو بعدم دوامه أو سكت عنهما والأخيران باطلان أما الثاني وهو تصريحه بعدم دوامه ( فلانه لو قال ذلك ) وصرح به ( لتواتر) عنه قطعاً ( لكونه من الأمور العظيمة التي تتوفر الدواعي على نقلها ) وإشاعتها ( سيما من الأعداء ومن يدعي نسخ دينه وذلك ) لأنه أقوى ( حجة (له ) أي لمن يدعيه ( فيه) أي في جواز نسخه فلا بد أن تتوفر دواعيه على نقله لكنه لم يتواتر إجماعاً . (وأما الثالث) وهو سكوته عنهما (فلانه يقتضي ثبوت دينه مرة واحدة وعدم تكرره لأن مقتضى الإطلاق يتحقق بالمرة الواحدة ( وأنه معلوم الانتفاء لتقرره إلى أوان النسخ إما بشريعة عيسى أو بشريعة محمد باتفاق بيننا وبينكم والجواب : منع تواتر (ذلك أي دوام السبت (من موسى عليه السلام ولو كان كذلك أي متواتر كما زعمتم ( لاحتج به على محمد ولو احتج به عليه ( لنقل ذلك الاحتجاج ( متواتراً) لتوفر الدواعي على نقله ولا تواتر أصلا كيف وقد اشتهر أنه اختلقه ابن الراوندي لليهود ) وأما الترديد فنختار منه ( أنه صرح بدوامه إلى ظهور الناسخ على لسان نبي يأتي من بعده ( وإنما لم ينقل ) ذلك ( تواتراً إما لقلة الدواعي ) منهم (إلى نقله لما فيه من الحجة عليهم) لا لهم ( قوله : ( ولك أن تحمل المحكوم عليه إلخ) هذا هو الظاهر لأن أحكام الإنجيل بقيت إلى ظهور دين الإسلام، ولا شك أن بعض الناس أدركوا كلا الحكمين في بداية الإسلام فإن قلت : اختلاف الفعلين المتعلقين للحكم الناسخ والمنسوخ وقد ثبت أن خبر نسخ الصلاة إلى بيت المقدس بلغ أهل قباء وهم في صلاة الظهر فتحولوا إلى الكعبة بلا نقض صلاتهم فالحد مورد الحكمين؟ قلت : بل اختلف موردهما باعتبار جزأي الصلاة . كيف يدعي قوله : ( وأما الثالث إلخ) فيه بحث لأن النص يدل على شرعية موجبة إلى زمان ظهور الناسخ . قوله : ( والجواب : منع تواتر ذلك) على أنه كثيراً ما يعبر بالتأبيد والدوام عن طول الزمان . وإما لقلة الناقلين في بعض الطبقات ( المعبرة كثرتها في التواتر ( لأن اليهود جرت لهم وقائع ردتهم إلى أقل القليل ممن لا يحصل التواتر بنقله ( كما في زمن بختنصر فإنه قتلهم وأفناهم إلا من شد منهم . وأما العيسوية من اليهود فطريق الرد عليهم أنهم لما سلموا صحة نبوته بالأدلة القاطعة والمعجزات الباهرة وجب عليهم أن يعترفوا بما تواتر عنه من دعواه البعثة إلى الأمم كافة لا إِلى العرب خاصة فإنه قد علم ذلك منه كما علم وجوده ودعواه الرسالة.
And this is for us and for you: that you may take the subject of judgment here as the act, for what the abrogating judgment pertains to of acts is different from what the abrogated judgment pertains to. Then abrogation is permissible in judgments related to the acts of a single person. Second, of the two aspects: that Moses, peace be upon him, negated the abrogation of his religion, and it is necessary to acknowledge his truthfulness because he is a prophet by agreement. Then there is no prophethood for one who claims its abrogation, and that is what is intended to be clarified, i.e., explaining that he negated the abrogation of his religion, and that it is mutawatir from him. His statement: they clung to the Sabbath as long as the heavens and earth endure. If the permanence of the Sabbath and the impossibility of its abrogation are established, then its abrogation is impossible in all its other rulings. Rather we say: what is meant by its permanence is the permanence of Judaism, as is understood spontaneously. Also, either Moses explicitly stated the permanence of his religion, or its non-permanence, or was silent about both; the last two are invalid. As for the second, which is his explicit statement of its non-permanence: because if he said that and explicitly stated it, it would necessarily be mutawatir from him, because it is among the great matters for which there are abundant motives to transmit it and publicize it, especially from enemies and those who claim abrogation of his religion, because it is the strongest proof for them in the permissibility of its abrogation, so there must be abundant motives for its transmission, but it is not mutawatir by consensus. As for the third, which is his silence about both: because it would necessitate the establishment of his religion once and its non-repetition, because the implication of absoluteness is achieved by one occurrence, and it is known to be false because it continued until the time of abrogation, either by the law of Jesus or by the law of Muhammad, by agreement between us and you. The answer: denial that this, i.e., the permanence of the Sabbath, is mutawatir from Moses, peace be upon him. If it were so, i.e., mutawatir as you claim, he would have used it as an argument against Muhammad, and if he had used it as an argument against him, that argumentation would have been transmitted mutawatir because of abundant motives for its transmission, and there is no tawatur at all. How indeed, and it is well-known that Ibn al-Rawandi fabricated it for the Jews. As for the disjunction, we choose from it that he explicitly stated its permanence until the appearance of an abrogator on the tongue of a prophet who comes after him. It was not transmitted mutawatir either because of the scarcity of motives among them to transmit it due to what it contains of proof against them, not for them. His statement: and you may take the subject of judgment etc. – this is apparent because the rulings of the Gospel remained until the appearance of the religion of Islam, and there is no doubt that some people encountered both rulings at the beginning of Islam. If you say: the two acts pertaining to the abrogating and abrogated judgment differ, and it is established that the news of the abrogation of prayer towards Jerusalem reached the people of Quba' while they were performing the noon prayer, so they turned to the Kaaba without nullifying their prayer, so the limit is the locus of the two judgments? I say: rather their loci differ with respect to the two parts of the prayer. How does he claim? His statement: as for the third etc. – there is discussion in it because the text indicates legislation positively until the time of the appearance of the abrogator. His statement: and the answer is denial of that being mutawatir – although often eternity and permanence are used to mean length of time. And either because of the scarcity of transmitters in some classes whose multiplicity is considered in tawatur, because the Jews experienced events that reduced them to the very few from whose transmission tawatur does not occur, as in the time of Nebuchadnezzar, for he killed them and annihilated them except a few who escaped. As for the 'Isawiyya among the Jews, the method of refuting them is that when they acknowledge the soundness of his prophethood by decisive proofs and dazzling miracles, they must acknowledge what is mutawatir from him of his claim of being sent to all nations, not to Arabs specifically, for that is known from him just as his existence and his claim of messengership are known.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Jewish arguments against the abrogation of the Mosaic law. The author provides a detailed response to two main points raised by Jewish opponents. First, he addresses the claim that Moses negated the abrogation of his religion, arguing that such a negation would have to be mutawatir (massively transmitted) to be accepted, but it is not. Second, he considers the three possibilities regarding Moses' statement: explicit permanence, explicit non-permanence, or silence. Both non-permanence and silence are deemed invalid; non-permanence would have been widely transmitted if stated, and silence would imply a single establishment of the religion, which contradicts its continuation until abrogation by Jesus or Muhammad. The author then denies the tawatur of the Sabbath's permanence, arguing that if it were true, Moses would have used it against Muhammad, and that would have been transmitted. He further notes that the argument was fabricated by Ibn al-Rawandi. The response also addresses the 'Isawiyya sect, who accept Muhammad's prophethood but limit it to Arabs; the author argues that since they accept his prophetic proofs, they must also accept his universally transmitted claim of universal mission. Throughout, the commentary follows the logical sequence of objection and answer, maintaining the author's argumentative structure.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh)
تواتر (tawatur)
دوام (dawam)
السبت (sabbath)
ابن الراوندي (Ibn al-Rawandi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the absence of transmitted proof automatically proves the claim.
Correction: Al-Jurjani argues that absence of tawatur when motives for transmission exist indicates the claim's falsehood.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Jurjani argue that Moses could not have explicitly stated the non-permanence of his religion?
A) Because Moses was forbidden to speak about abrogation
B) Because such a statement would have been mutawatir due to its importance, but it is not
C) Because the Torah explicitly forbids abrogation
D) Because the Jews would have hidden it

Key Takeaway
Al-Jurjani demonstrates that claims about prophetic statements must be supported by tawatur, and their absence disproves the Jewish argument against abrogation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim about a prophet that seems to support a comfortable belief, do you check whether it has been reliably transmitted? How many times have you accepted a 'famous' story without verifying its tawatur? What does that say about your commitment to truth?
?
The enemies of Moses had every motive to transmit his words if he had denied abrogation, yet no such report exists. Reflect: Are there truths in your life—about your own faults or neglected duties—that you avoid speaking or acting on because they are uncomfortable? What would change if you treated those truths with the same urgency as the enemies of Moses?
?
Al-Jurjani dismisses silence as impossible because the religion continued. Is there an area of your faith where you have been silent, assuming a one-time act is enough—like a single prayer or charity—when Allah demands ongoing commitment? What one step will you take today to break that silence and embrace steadfastness?

Consensus and Disagreement on Prophetic Infallibility
Al-Jurjani explains consensus and disagreement on prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ʿiṣma), including the consensus on infallibility from deliberate lies and disbelief, the disagreement on forgetfulness, and the rationale behind these positions.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible in conveying revelation, but scholars disagree on forgetfulness.

This lesson examines the central doctrine of prophetic infallibility. Al-Jurjani explains that all religions agree prophets cannot deliberately lie in matters confirmed by miracles, but there is disagreement on whether unintentional errors are possible. The passage also addresses infallibility from disbelief and a deviant sectarian view, culminating in an objection and answer that reinforces the miracle's scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic and English translation to get an overview. Notice the structure: consensus, then disagreement, then other sins, and finally an objection and answer.
The passage begins with 'المقصد الخامس'.
2
Understand the consensus on deliberate lies
Identify the unanimous agreement that prophets cannot deliberately lie in matters attested by miracles. Ask: why would lying nullify the miracle?
The reason is that if they could lie, the miracle would lose its evidentiary power.
3
Examine the disagreement on forgetfulness
Contrast the views of Abu Ishaq and Qadi Abu Bakr. One argues that the miracle guarantees truthfulness in all conveyance, the other limits it to deliberate actions.
This disagreement is about the scope of the miracle's indication.
4
Explore infallibility from other sins and the Azariqa
Note the consensus on infallibility from disbelief and the deviant view of the Azariqa who considered all sins as disbelief, thus allowing the possibility of a prophet disbelieving.
The Azariqa are a Kharijite sect.
5
Review the objection and answer about the miracle
Read the final exchange where an objection is raised and answered, reinforcing that the miracle testifies to truthfulness in all deliberate conveyance.
This clarifies the earlier reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الخامس : في عصمة الأنبياء أجمع أهل الملل والشرائع كلها ( على ) وجوب ( عصمتهم عن تعمد الكذب فيما دل المعجز) القاطع ( على صدقهم فيه كدعوى الرسالة وما يبلغونه عن الله ) إلى الخلائق إذ لو جاز عليهم التقول والافتراء في ذلك عقلا لأدى إلى إبطال دلالة المعجزة وهو محال ( وفي جواز صدوره أي صدور الكذب ( عنهم ) فيما ذكر (على سبيل ) السهو والنسيان خلاف فمنعه (الأستاذ ( أبو إسحاق ( وكثير من الأئمة الأعلام ( لدلالة المعجزة على صدقهم في تبليغ الأحكام فلو جاز الخلف في ذلك لكان نقضاً للدلالة المعجزة وهو ممتنع وجوزه القاضي ) أبو بكر ( مصيراً منه إلى عدم دخوله في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة ) فإن المعجزة إنما دلت على صدقه فيما هو متذكر له عامد وإليه وأما ما كان من النسيان وفلتات اللسان فلا دلالة لها على الصدق فيه فلا يلزم من الكذب هناك نقض لدلالتها . ( وأما سائر الذنوب ) يعني به ما الكذب في التبليغ ) فهي إما كفر أو غيره ) من المعاصي . ( وأما الكفر فأجمعت الأمة على عصمتهم منه قبل النبوة وبعدها ولا خلاف لأحد منهم في ذلك ( غير أن الأزارقة من الخوارج جوزوا عليهم الذنب وكل ذنب عندهم كفر فلزمهم تجویز الكفر ، بل يحكى عنهم أنهم قالوا بجواز بعثة نبي علم الله تعالى أنه يكفر بعد نبوته قوله : (كما في زمن بختنصر) قيل عليه : إن بختنصر إنما قتل يهود الشام وبيت المقدس وهم كانوا منتشرين في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها اللهم إلا أن يمنع انتشارهم في ذلك الزمان . قوله : ( لأدى إلى إبطال دلالة المعجزة قيل : لا نسلم أن الكذب فيما سوى دعوى الرسالة مما يبلغونه إلى الخلائق يؤدى إلى إبطال دلالة المعجزة، فإن المعجزة إنما تدل على صدقه في نفس دعوى الرسالة أو فيما يبلغه عن الله تعالى مقروناً بدعوى النبوة المقرونة بإظهار المعجزة وجوابه ما مر من أن الخارق لا يظهر على يد من يكذب عمداً فالمعجزة تدل على صدقه في جميع ما يبلغه الله تعالى حالاً واستقبالاً . عن
The Fifth Purpose: On the Infallibility of the Prophets. The people of all religions and laws have unanimously agreed on the obligation of their infallibility from deliberate lying in that which the decisive miracle indicates their truthfulness in, such as the claim of messengership and what they convey from God to creation, because if lying and fabrication were rationally possible for them in that, it would lead to nullifying the indication of the miracle, and that is impossible. And concerning the permissibility of its occurrence, i.e., lying, from them in what was mentioned, by way of forgetfulness and oversight, there is disagreement. Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and many of the eminent imams forbid it, because the miracle indicates their truthfulness in conveying judgments; if discrepancy were permissible in that, it would be a violation of the indication of the miracle, and that is impossible. The judge Abu Bakr permitted it, taking the position that it is not included in the attestation intended by the miracle, for the miracle only indicates his truthfulness in what he is mindful of and intentional about. As for what is due to forgetfulness and slips of the tongue, there is no indication of truthfulness in it, so lying there does not necessitate a violation of its indication. As for the rest of sins, meaning by it other than lying in conveyance, they are either disbelief or other than that of sins. As for disbelief, the entire community has unanimously agreed on their infallibility from it before prophethood and after it, and there is no disagreement among anyone in that, except that the Azariqa of the Khawarij permitted sin for them, and every sin in their view is disbelief, so they necessarily permitted disbelief. Rather it is narrated from them that they said it is permissible to send a prophet whom God knows will disbelieve after his prophethood. His statement: as in the time of Nebuchadnezzar – it was objected to him: Nebuchadnezzar only killed the Jews of Syria and Jerusalem, and they were scattered in the east and west of the earth, unless one prevents their spread at that time. His statement: would lead to nullifying the indication of the miracle – it is said: We do not accept that lying in other than the claim of messengership of what they convey to creation would lead to nullifying the indication of the miracle, for the miracle only indicates his truthfulness in the claim of messengership itself or in what he conveys from God, Most High, coupled with the claim of prophethood coupled with the manifestation of the miracle. And its answer is what has passed: that the extraordinary act does not appear at the hand of one who lies intentionally, so the miracle indicates his truthfulness in all that he conveys from God, Most High, present and future.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses the doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ʿiṣma). It begins by stating that there is consensus across all religions on the obligation of prophets being infallible from deliberate falsehood in matters attested by a decisive miracle, such as the claim of prophethood and the conveyance of divine messages. The reason is that if lying were possible, the miracle's evidentiary force would be nullified. Then it introduces a disagreement: whether prophets can accidentally lie (through forgetfulness or oversight). Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and many scholars forbid it, arguing that the miracle confirms truthfulness in all conveyance; any error would undermine it. Qadi Abu Bakr permits it, arguing that the miracle only guarantees truthfulness in deliberate, mindful statements, not in unintentional slips. The passage then addresses other sins, distinguishing between disbelief (kufr) and other sins. There is complete consensus that prophets are protected from disbelief both before and after prophethood, except the Azariqa (a Kharijite sect) who considered all sins as disbelief and thus allowed the possibility of a prophet disbelieving after prophethood. A marginal comment clarifies that the miracle's indication extends to all that the prophet deliberately conveys, as an extraordinary act cannot occur at the hand of one who intentionally lies. The commentary follows the sequence: consensus on deliberate lies, disagreement on forgetfulness, consensus on disbelief, and the deviant view of the Azariqa.

Key Terms
عصمة (ʿiṣma)
المعجزة (muʿjiza)
سهو (sahw)
نسيان (nisyan)
الأزارقة (Azariqa)
كفر (kufr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic infallibility covers all actions, including unintentional errors.
Correction: There is disagreement; some scholars permit forgetfulness and slips of the tongue, as the passage shows.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for the consensus that prophets cannot deliberately lie in matters attested by miracles?
A) Because lying would contradict their moral character
B) Because it would nullify the evidence of the miracle
C) Because the Torah prohibits lying
D) Because they are incapable of lying

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in deliberate conveyance of revelation, but the possibility of forgetfulness is disputed, and they are unanimously protected from disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that prophets are infallible from deliberate lying in conveying revelation, but some scholars permit forgetfulness. How does this distinction change the way you rely on every word of the Quran and Sunnah? Will you now examine your own inadvertent slips in conveying Islamic knowledge, and what steps will you take to ensure you are as careful as possible in teaching others?
?
The Azariqa believed a prophet could commit kufr after prophethood, a view rejected by consensus. Yet, do you ever act as if some of Allah's commands are not essential, or prioritize worldly desires over divine orders? In what area of your life are you effectively 'disbelieving' by disobedience, and how will you repent and reaffirm your absolute trust in the Prophet's ﷺ teaching?
?
The objection raised in the passage questions whether the miracle covers all that the prophet conveys. Reflect: Do you selectively accept parts of the prophetic message while doubting others due to personal discomfort? This lesson demands that the miracle attests to truthfulness in all deliberate conveyance. What command or prohibition do you find hardest to submit to, and how can you strengthen your conviction that it is truly from Allah?

Response to the Objection of Insufficient Transmitters
Sanusi addresses the objection of insufficient transmitters and defends the example of Nebuchadnezzar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jewish objection regarding insufficient transmitters for the Prophet's claim to universal prophethood is refuted using the concept of tawatur and the historical example of Nebuchadnezzar's massacre.

Core Idea
Even if transmitters are few in some layers, the overall transmission remains mutawatir.

Sanusi addresses a Jewish objection that the chain of transmission for the Prophet's claim to be sent to all nations is too weak. He explains that although historical events like the massacre by Nebuchadnezzar reduced the number of Jewish transmitters, the principle of tawatur—widespread transmission—still holds. The marginal commentary defends this example against the critique that the Jews were not all killed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation.
First, read the original Arabic text and its English translation to get a sense of the argument.
Notice the structure: objection, response, and a clarification.
2
Identify the Jewish objection.
The Jews claimed that the transmitters in some layers are too few for tawatur. Find where this is stated.
The text mentions 'قلة الناقلين في بعض الطبقات'.
3
Understand the response using historical events.
Sanusi points to historical events like Nebuchadnezzar's killing of many Jews, which reduced their numbers. However, this does not negate tawatur from the Muslim side.
The response is that the reduction affected Jewish transmitters, but the Muslim transmission remains strong.
4
Analyze the marginal defense of the Nebuchadnezzar example.
The text includes a counter-objection that Nebuchadnezzar only killed Jews in Syria and Jerusalem, not all. Consider how this is answered.
The response is that perhaps the Jews were not widely spread at that time.

The First Observatory - The Fifth Objective: On the Inerrancy of the Prophets. (And either due to the paucity of transmitters in some layers (the number of which is considered abundant for tawatur (because the Jews had events that reduced them to a very small number whose transmission does not attain tawatur (as in the time of Nebuchadnezzar, for he killed them and annihilated them except for a few who fled from them. And as for the 'Isawiyya among the Jews, the way to refute them is that when they accept the soundness of his prophethood by definitive proofs and overwhelming miracles, they must acknowledge what has been transmitted mutawatir from him of his claim of mission to all nations, not to the Arabs specifically, for that is known from him just as his existence and his claim of message are known. His saying: (as in the time of Nebuchadnezzar) It was said upon it: Indeed Nebuchadnezzar only killed the Jews of Syria and Jerusalem, and they were scattered in the East and West of the earth, unless it is said that their spread in that time was prevented. Commentary
This passage is a response to a Jewish objection regarding the transmission of the Prophet's claim to be sent to all nations. The author first addresses the objection that the chain of transmitters in some layers is too few for tawatur, explaining that historical events like Nebuchadnezzar's massacres reduced the number of Jewish transmitters. Then he refutes the 'Isawiyya sect specifically: since they accept the Prophet's prophethood based on definitive proofs and miracles, they must accept the mutawatir reports that he claimed universal mission, just as they accept his existence and his claim of prophecy. The marginal commentary clarifies two points: first, the example of Nebuchadnezzar is defended against the objection that the Jews were widespread; second, an objection that the miracle only proves truthfulness in the specific claim of prophethood, not in every report, is answered by the principle that a miracle never occurs on the hand of a deliberate liar, so it proves truthfulness in all his revealed messages.

بختنصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A reduction in transmitters in one generation completely invalidates tawatur.
Correction: Historical accidents that reduce a community's population do not break the tawatur from another community (Muslims).

Checkpoint
What historical event does the author cite to explain the reduction in Jewish transmitters?
A) The Babylonian exile
B) The massacre by Nebuchadnezzar
C) The Roman destruction of Jerusalem
D) The plague

Key Takeaway
Historical reductions in a community's population do not negate the reliability of mutawatir transmission from another community.

?

?
Imagine the Jewish community after Nebuchadnezzar's attack—only a few survivors. If you were among them, would you still be willing to carry the truth forward? What does that say about your responsibility to uphold and transmit this deen even when you feel alone?

Prophet's Universal Mission Accepted by Miracles
Sanusi refutes the 'Isawiyya Jews by showing that accepting the Prophet's miracles requires accepting his universal mission, and clarifies the scope of miracle's indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the 'Isawiyya Jews are refuted: their acceptance of the Prophet's miracles requires them to accept the mutawatir claim of universal mission, and that the miracle proves truthfulness in all conveyed messages.

Core Idea
If you accept the Prophet's miracles, you must accept all his mutawatir claims, including universal mission.

Sanusi then turns to a specific Jewish sect, the 'Isawiyya, who accept the Prophet's prophethood based on miracles but rejected his claim to be sent to all nations. The author argues that since they accept his prophethood through definitive proofs, they must accept the mutawatir reports of his universal mission. He also addresses an objection about the scope of miracles: they prove truthfulness in all that he conveys from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the 'Isawiyya.
Focus on the argument that acceptance of prophethood implies acceptance of mutawatir claims.
Look for the phrase 'لما سلموا صحة نبوته بالأدلة القاطعة'.
2
Understand the scope of the miracle's indication.
There is an objection that the miracle only proves truthfulness in the specific claim of prophethood, not in every report. The answer is that the miracle indicates truthfulness in all that the prophet conveys from Allah.
The principle: 'الخارق لا يظهر على يد من يكذب عمداً'.
3
Reflect on the logical necessity.
The passage shows that accepting the foundational proof (miracles) necessitates accepting all related mutawatir reports.
This is a common theological reasoning.

Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Jewish objection regarding the transmission of the Prophet's claim to be sent to all nations. The author first addresses the objection that the chain of transmitters in some layers is too few for tawatur, explaining that historical events like Nebuchadnezzar's massacres reduced the number of Jewish transmitters. Then he refutes the 'Isawiyya sect specifically: since they accept the Prophet's prophethood based on definitive proofs and miracles, they must accept the mutawatir reports that he claimed universal mission, just as they accept his existence and his claim of prophecy. The marginal commentary clarifies two points: first, the example of Nebuchadnezzar is defended against the objection that the Jews were widespread; second, an objection that the miracle only proves truthfulness in the specific claim of prophethood, not in every report, is answered by the principle that a miracle never occurs on the hand of a deliberate liar, so it proves truthfulness in all his revealed messages.

Key Terms
عيسوية
بعثة
معجزة
صدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The miracle only witnesses to the truth of the specific claim of prophethood, not to other statements.
Correction: A miracle is performed only by a truthful messenger; thus it attests to his truthfulness in all that he conveys from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why must the 'Isawiyya Jews accept the Prophet's universal mission?
A) Because they are monotheists.
B) Because they accept his prophethood by miracles.
C) Because they are from a specific sect.
D) Because the claim is in the Torah.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance of a prophet's miracles logically entails acceptance of all mutawatir claims made by that prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The 'Isawiyya accepted the Prophet’s miracles but rejected his universal mission. Is there any area of your faith where you are similarly selective—accepting what feels easy and rejecting what feels difficult? What would it cost you to be consistent, and are you willing to pay that price?

Definition of Prophetic Inerrancy in Deliberate Falsehood
Definition of prophetic inerrancy and disagreement on forgetfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of prophetic inerrancy: the consensus that prophets cannot deliberately lie, and the scholarly disagreement on whether forgetfulness is exempted.

Core Idea
Prophets are preserved from deliberate falsehood, but forgetfulness is debated.

This lesson examines the foundational principle of prophetic inerrancy (ʿiṣma). The author first states the unanimous agreement that prophets cannot deliberately lie in matters confirmed by miracles, such as their message. Then he presents a key disagreement: some scholars extend inerrancy to unintentional errors from forgetfulness, while others limit it to intentional acts. Understanding this debate clarifies the precise scope of prophetic protection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the clear structure: first the consensus, then the disagreement introduced by 'And regarding...'.
The phrase 'أجمع أهل الملل' signals consensus.
2
Identify the two positions on forgetfulness
Find the views of al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq (prohibiting forgetfulness) and al-Qadi Abu Bakr (permitting it). Notice how each argues from the miracle's indication.
The key difference lies in what the miracle is taken to attest.
3
Ask why this matters
Reflect on why the debate over forgetfulness is significant: it affects how we understand the reliability of prophetic transmissions. If a prophet could forget, does that undermine trust in revelation?
This connects to the broader doctrine of ʿiṣma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجمع أهل الملل والشرائع كلها على وجوب عصمتهم عن تعمد الكذب فيما دل المعجز القاطع على صدقهم فيه كدعوى الرسالة وما يبلغونه عن الله إلى الخلائق إذ لو جاز عليهم التقول والافتراء في ذلك عقلا لأدى إلى إبطال دلالة المعجزة وهو محال ( وفي جواز صدوره أي صدور الكذب عنهم فيما ذكر على سبيل السهو والنسيان خلاف فمنعه الأستاذ أبو إسحاق وكثير من الأئمة الأعلام لدلالة المعجزة على صدقهم في تبليغ الأحكام فلو جاز الخلف في ذلك لكان نقضاً للدلالة المعجزة وهو ممتنع وجوزه القاضي أبو بكر مصيراً منه إلى عدم دخوله في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة فإن المعجزة إنما دلت على صدقه فيما هو متذكر له عامد وإليه وأما ما كان من النسيان وفلتات اللسان فلا دلالة لها على الصدق فيه فلا يلزم من الكذب هناك نقض لدلالتها.
All people of religions and laws are in consensus on the necessity of their inerrancy from deliberate falsehood in what the definitive miracle indicates their truthfulness in, such as the claim of message and what they convey from God to the creatures, for if it were rationally possible for them to invent and fabricate in that, it would lead to nullifying the indication of the miracle, which is impossible. And regarding the permissibility of its occurrence (i.e., falsehood) from them in what was mentioned, by way of forgetfulness and oversight, there is disagreement. Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and many of the eminent imams prohibited it, due to the miracle's indication of their truthfulness in conveying the rulings, so if variance were permissible in that, it would be a contradiction of the miracle's indication, which is impossible. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr permitted it, based on his view that it is not included in the attestation intended by the miracle, for the miracle only indicates his truthfulness in what he is mindful of and deliberate about, but as for what is from forgetfulness and slips of the tongue, there is no indication of truthfulness in it, so falsehood there does not entail contradiction of its indication.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of prophetic inerrancy. It begins with the consensus that prophets are necessarily inerrant regarding deliberate falsehood in matters that the miracle confirms their truthfulness, such as the claim of prophethood and the messages they convey. If they could deliberately lie, the miracle would lose its indicative power. Then it presents a disagreement about unintentional falsehood (forgetfulness and oversight). Al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and many scholars hold that such falsehood is also impossible because the miracle attests to their truthfulness in conveying rulings, so any error would undermine that attestation. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr argues that the miracle only confirms truthfulness in what is intentional and mindful; forgetfulness is not included, so falsehood from forgetfulness does not contradict the miracle.

Key Terms
عصمة
معجزة
سهو
نسيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All falsehood from prophets is equally impossible; there is no nuance.
Correction: While deliberate falsehood is universally prohibited, there is a valid scholarly dispute about unintentional falsehood from forgetfulness, as the passage shows.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qadi Abu Bakr, why is falsehood from forgetfulness not a contradiction of the miracle?
A) Because the miracle does not indicate truthfulness in forgetful states.
B) Because prophets never forget.
C) Because the miracle is not definitive.
D) Because forgetfulness is not possible for prophets.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic inerrancy is certain in deliberate falsehood, but scholars differ on unintentional errors from forgetfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The lesson shows that miracle confirms truthfulness in deliberate statements. In your own life, when you speak about Islam, are you deliberate and mindful, or do you sometimes speak carelessly? How can this lesson hold you accountable to be more conscious of your words?
